Spring and Autumn

Death 211

— Zuo Yun

Death, what a dark, miserable, and decadent word! If you say that someone has died, how sad you are for him, and at the same time, there is a sense of reality that makes you feel that everything is empty. Or someone and you enter! "I'm going to die!" How shocked and surprised you are, you must try your best to stop him from this attempt. Therefore, death is the enemy of all living things. People certainly curse it, and no other animals are willing to avoid it. But there is a stubborn devil!! Death, for everything is never compromised, never tolerant, so the tragedy of mankind is doomed. So the stage of life often has a touching performance. Regardless of wealth or poverty, the advent of death is unstoppable, and at the same time, everyone will inevitably encounter this ending. The greatness and power of death can be seen from here. It does not have the snobbery, flattery, and inequality of the present society. Regardless of intelligence, foolishness, worthiness, or unworthiness, its treatment is the same. However, in my observation, it may be a little more abusive to the rich, which is very obvious in medical treatment. Because the rich have a lot of money, when they are sick, dozens of doctors come to their door every day. Not to mention that the patient's spirit is disturbed, but also that many bitter medicines increase the patient's pain. This is not my nonsense, there are many examples. Recently, there was a rich man whose six-year-old grandson was sick for more than 20 days, and the medical expenses cost more than 20,000 yuan, but in the end, he was taken away by the god of death. Although the children of the poor do not have the pain of excessive medical treatment, they often have to die. The god of death cannot but be said to be very fair in this regard. However, the word death is ultimately the most terrifying noun in the world. Now that science is advocated, there is still no way to deal with death. No matter how advanced science is, it is ultimately no match for the ferocity of the god of death, so people often understand each other under the threat of death. In fact, you will fight for the world in this life, and when the god of death comes, you will still have nothing. There are also people who do not die, that is, when he was alive, he created a lot of happiness for human society. Although his body is dead, his spirit still exists in the world. Only this kind of person is immortal. After all, there are very few immortal people. However, this immortal life is indeed needed by society, so I hope that human beings will not die!

Not Funny 212

— Mu Yin

"Not funny is not funny, crying is real crying"

When the boss sees the employee, the employee sees the laborer, a burst of smile must suddenly emerge on everyone's face. The laborer sees the employee, in order to please him, he smiles first. The employee sees the laborer, helplessly retracts his shoulders, and opens the corners of his mouth, barely making out what seems to be a smile. In this exchange of smiles, there is only cold air, not the joy of a son seeing his father, or the smile of a sister hugging her younger brother, but just showing each other's hideous faces. The boss sees the customer, the customer sees the boss, they nod, smile, and sit down to talk about business. The business is over, the customer leaves, and they smile at each other again. The first smile is relatively hopeful, and the smile is more forceful. The latter smile has no strength left, just a cold sinking. The procuress holds the hand of the patron, long sentence, short sentence, constantly giggling, the patron is smiled upon, and then goes to see the prostitute's even deeper flattery smile, the smile is smiled, and the smile covers the world with a black curtain. Not only that, unnatural smiles can be seen everywhere in the world, within a square foot, including the ferociousness of wild beasts and the flattery of foxes.

On the Old Book Stall 213

— Rong Yu

I feel a lack of knowledge, and I often want to buy some books to read. A new book is published, and it always costs several yuan, which makes the poor scholar look away. Sometimes I spend some money and buy a big bag of books back, and my children laugh at me for being old and confused, but my old wife mutters, "What's the use of buying these things? They can't keep you warm in the cold, and they can't feed you when you're hungry!" I also try to defend myself: "First, it's good for me to pass the time; second, I can pass it on to my children." My wife laughs and says: "I've only heard of not knowing people, it's not good to eat; but I haven't heard of not knowing words and starving to death!" I have no sufficient reason to refute. However, loving books is my hobby. To be economical, I can only go to the old book stall to search. Speaking of the old book stall, it used to be gathered in the City God Temple. If you have sharp eyes and pay a cheap price, you can buy some good copies. However, since many sophisticated students specialize in buying old textbooks in old bookstores, I bought these four books back, and after reading them, I couldn't help but have some small feelings: people in the past liked to copy books, but people today are unwilling to do such stupid things. People in the past liked to criticize and circle points in books, but people today are unwilling to dirty the books. After all, people today are smarter than people in the past, so they are unwilling to do so. I think in a few years, handwritten copies may be completely extinct.

Winter Dusk 215

— Li Junsi

After a miserable cold rain, the climate obviously turned cold suddenly, especially in the evening. The wind on the street lifted the corners of the robes, and scraped against the body, involuntarily shivering several times. I deeply felt that the cotton robe that was daunting in summer was lovely, and I also felt slightly thinner. In the lights all over the street, women's necks seemed to be shortened by a section, deeply buried in the fur collar of their coats. Men also seemed to have incurable carbuncles growing on their necks, wearing scarves, or even turning up the high collars of their coats. Even if they didn't, everyone subconsciously held their hands, shrunk their necks, and prevented the invasion of the cold wind. Only the rickshaw pullers and the like were still facing the cold wind, panting hot air, pulling dignified people, and striding forward, as if they were born without feeling and did not know cold and heat. Along with the cold wind, the urgent and sharp sound of selling evening newspapers filled the streets and alleys, making people suddenly realize the sorrow of life. Walking past the door of a pawnshop, looking inside, I saw several haggard people standing outside the dense iron fence and the high counter under the bright lights, wondering whether they were mortgaging clothes or redeeming clothes. In the end, was it for clothes? Or was it for food? However, whether it was mortgaging or redeeming, they were all equally pitiful! The mood of dusk became more and more lonely and bleak. Only the radios of several department stores were singing various farcical songs to cater to low-level tastes, "It's also the sound squeezed out of life!" I thought.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 216

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 23

The pain is unbearable, listen intently to the drums and music

The joy has not been fulfilled, hasten to bid farewell to the flying talisman

Zhao Ziqiang silently went over and wrung out a towel, handing it to Guizhi with both hands. Guizhi smiled in a low voice and said: I can't afford this. You're welcome, I'll wash it. He had already changed his clothes. At this time, he rolled up his two small sleeves high, revealing two white and round arms. He took the towel and stood by the dressing table to wash his hands and face. Zhao Ziqiang stood behind him, watching for a while with a slight smile, and then took out the scented soap, snow cream, face powder, and rouge cream from the dressing table drawer, one by one, and placed them on the table. Guizhi smiled and said to him: My husband, how do you understand these? Let me do it myself. Zhao Ziqiang smiled and said: You're tired today, I have to serve you. Guizhi looked at the door of the room, and seeing that the curtain was down, he said: You're tired too, shouldn't I serve you? Ziqiang smiled and said: I can't afford it. But if you really want to serve me... Guizhi. Reached out and grabbed his mouth and said: That's enough, don't say any more. Ziqiang took the opportunity to hold his hand and sniffed it for a while. Because he heard Zhao Weng's cough in the outer room, he quietly walked away. But he didn't want to walk away either. He walked to the bed and saw the snow-white bedspread and a bed of light blue and pink silk quilt. He felt that the colors were particularly harmonious. The four white pillowcases embroidered with small red flowers were also particularly attractive. So he leaned on the bed with his pillows, sighed slightly, and smiled: I really can't avoid being short of heroic spirit and long on children's affection. Guizhi was still washing his face, not making a sound. Zhao Ziqiang then pulled a pillow and hugged it in his arms, constantly smelling it with his nose on the pillow. Guizhi said: What's wrong with you? Are you crazy? Zhao Ziqiang smiled and said: You just said that this is the only thing in your life. The days after the wedding are called honeymoon, don't you know? (234) . So their gaze was focused on Western books and various textbooks. They also changed their name to old bookstore. North Sichuan Road, Cade Road, and Ximen all have them. The price of books is really not cheap. I once bought a "Collection of European and American Short Essays," and it was a pirated version. The original price was three and a half yuan, and it was sold for two and a half yuan. I also went to buy an "Outline of Political Science." This book has been published for a long time, and it is out of date. The original price was one and a half yuan, and it was sold for one yuan. Now, the old bookstore mainly deals in Western books, so it does not pay attention to Chinese ancient books. If you want to buy this kind of book in an old bookstore, it is really difficult to find. Even if there is, the price is also very considerable! Last Sunday, I happened to walk to the Old West Gate. After flipping through it for a while at the old book stall on the roadside, I found several handwritten copies: one is "The Collection of Ouyang Wenzhonggong," the handwriting is very neat, and the cinnabar circle points are almost everywhere. One is "Du Zimei's Poetry Selection," the handwriting is not good, but there are comments. It is "Selected Essays of the Five Dynasties," the handwriting is good, and the selection is also precise. There is also an essay signed with the name "Gu Lin." I actually know what generation and where this old gentleman is from? These four books must be unpopular goods, and no one cares about them, so he sold them to me for eight cents.

Short Story

Three New Year's Eves (Middle) 217

— Shen Yan

Cheng Yuan was, as usual, wearing a camel hair robe with several buttons missing, and a dark green Zhigong呢 vest, with his round head bowed, eating his usual dinner with relish.｜A bowl of Luozhe (diced meat) noodles. "Little Li, be careful, there's water in that orange! Don't get your leather cloak dirty"｜Wu Baojun warned Li Yun with a pitying tone. Indeed, Li Yun was really dressed too carefully. Standing in the middle of these furniture and these two early guests, he was really like a phoenix. "Old Wu, it's New Year's Eve today, how do you have time to come here to chat?" Li Yun knew that Cheng Yuan was a famous poor boy. He incubated in this Longhu magazine almost all day, and sometimes slept on those piles of old magazines. So Li Yun didn't pay attention to him: but he thought that Wu Baojun's appearance in the seat was very strange. Because on ordinary days when the newspaper doesn't stop publishing, Old Wu is still frolicking and has no time. What's more, there is no newspaper as usual on this New Year's Eve. Why did he turn the cart before the horse and tidy up? "Haha! You are living too comfortably! Precisely because today is New Year's Eve, I came here" ! Saying that, Old Wu had already taken out a stack of invoices that were an inch thick from his tattered coat pocket, and waved it at Li Yun. Only then did Li Yun understand. "Poor fellow" ! Li Yun secretly laughed at him. Because although he himself usually lived an absurd and extravagant life like Wu Baojun, because of his environment, he had never tasted the bitterness of being surrounded by bill collectors on New Year's Eve. At that time, Cheng Yuan had already finished eating all the Luozhe noodles, including the soup, and was counting more than a dozen copper coins that had been smoothed. "A'Er, please fill up three copper coins for me, I'll pay you back tomorrow" ! He waved his hand to the waiter with a sallow face, half like a request, half like an order. "It's seven in total, including the day before yesterday" ! A'Er reluctantly took away the bowl and chopsticks, and reluctantly accepted Cheng Yuan's request. Li Yun looked at him and smiled slightly, and then threw a duck gizzard to him. (2) Three years ago New Year's Eve has arrived again. The New Year's Eve mentioned here is still the thirtieth night of the twelfth lunar month, because although the revolution was successful, the old habits of the Chinese people who cherish the old days are still unable to be changed. At about twelve o'clock, two steel-wire rickshaws were rolling westward on N Road, which was, as usual, crowded with people. "Old Cheng, I'm sorry! I've broken your money tonight" ! Li Yun, still wearing a suit and a velvet hat, looked back from the rickshaw in front and apologized to Cheng Yuan in the car behind. Tonight, Cheng Yuan hosted a dinner, inviting Li Yun to go to Kuaihuolin to eat Western food. After dinner, everyone originally planned to go to see a movie again, but because there was no money left in Li Yun's wallet, only ten or so invoices that could barely be pieced together were paid. So the result was that Cheng Yuan was the host again. Cheng Yuan is no longer writing articles, and is working as an assistant to a great lawyer.

Ministry of Education Stops Running

Order Regarding Night Classes at Five Shanghai Colleges 219

Night Classes Should Be Changed to Supplementary in Nature

(Nanjing, 30th) The Ministry of Education has ordered the Shanghai private Soochow and Shanghai Baptist Universities, the National Shanghai College of Commerce, and the private Chih Tze College of Law and Political Science to abolish their night classes. The original order stated roughly that, according to reports from inspectors of the Ministry, all the colleges and universities running night classes are in the fields of law and commerce. The classes are generally held from 4:30 PM to 11:00 PM, with four or five classes. The majority of the students have jobs during the day. It has been found that students who work during the day and attend classes at night do not have enough time for self-study outside of class for subjects that require it, and they have no time to rest from morning to night, which affects their energy. On the school side, the prescribed curriculum, apart from indoor lectures, cannot implement military training, physical education, and extracurricular activities. Students each have their own jobs and cannot be restricted to living on campus, making it impossible to strictly implement educational management. Among these students with jobs, there are indeed some who come to study because they feel they lack knowledge, but there are also those who are simply registering for a diploma. Since these night classes are not in line with the regulations of school education and the drawbacks are too numerous to mention, the Ministry specifically orders that these colleges and universities must not recruit new night class students or transfer students from the date of this document. The colleges and universities should formulate their own methods to conclude the studies of current students, and submit a detailed list of the names of the night class students to the Ministry for record, and they must not be reported together with the undergraduate students. If members of society truly have a need to seek specialized knowledge outside of their daytime work, they should only set up night classes of a supplementary nature, and should not overcharge tuition. Each evening class should not exceed three hours. Upon completion of the supplementary courses, a certificate of completion should be issued, and they should not be treated the same as students in formal schools. It is hereby ordered that you comply with these instructions and report back for verification.

General Meeting of Peking University Alumni Association in Nanjing 220

(Nanjing, 30th) The Nanjing Peking University Alumni Association will hold a general meeting of members in Nanjing at 6 PM on the 31st to re-elect executive and supervisory committee members, hold a spring dinner, discuss the construction of a clubhouse, and welcome former President Cai Yuanpei and his wife.

Current Situation of Education in Jiangxi Province (II) 221

｜Report by Special Commissioner of the Ministry of Education, Li Ximou｜

5. Situation of Local Education Funding and

Suggestions for Rectification

The local education funding in Jiangxi Province has suffered losses over the years due to banditry, and annual revenue has decreased. It is extremely difficult to collect statistics on education in the bandit-affected areas. According to the report from the Department of Education, the total local education funding for the province in the 20th year of the Republic (1931) was only over 730,000 yuan. The statistics on the sources and expenditures of local education funding in each county of Jiangxi Province in the 20th year of the Republic are attached below. (A) "Statistics on the Sources of Education Funding in Each County of Jiangxi Province": The sources of education funding in the 52 counties of Jiangxi Province are divided into five categories: (1) Land tax surcharges totaling 403,889 yuan; (2) Income from school properties, 184,608 yuan; (3) Additional and special levies, 84,286 yuan; (4) Other income, 66,112 yuan, totaling 738,895 yuan. (B) "Statistics on the Expenditures of Education Funding in Each County of Jiangxi Province": The expenditures of education funding in the 52 counties of Jiangxi Province are divided into four categories: (1) Total educational administrative expenses, 135,290 yuan; (2) School education expenses, 543,146 yuan; (3) Social education expenses, 48,388 yuan; (4) Temporary and miscellaneous expenses, 42,791 yuan, totaling 769,615 yuan. The Department of Education of Jiangxi Province has the following opinions regarding the rectification and planning of local education funding: (A) Regarding rectification: (1) "Investigate Educational Properties": Forms were created and repeatedly ordered to be filled out and reported by each county, and provincial school supervisors were instructed to strictly assess the situation during their inspections of education in each county. The counties have now successively filled out the forms and sent them to the Department, which will compile the statistics once they are all received. (2) "Review Education Funding Budgets": The budget for the income and expenditure of education funding for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933) in each county, except for bandit areas, have mostly been sent to the Department for review and have been approved or rejected accordingly. At the same time, the Department of Finance also sends personnel to participate when reviewing local funding budgets. In addition, the Department has stipulated standards for education administrative expenses, divided into three grades (Grade A bureau chiefs receive 80 yuan per month, Grade B 70 yuan, and Grade C 60 yuan), which are listed in a separate table with explanations. (3) "Strictly Prohibit the Misappropriation of Education Funding": In accordance with the measures to guarantee local education funding, each county has been notified to comply. Cases of misappropriation that have already occurred, such as the Chongren County government's plan to misappropriate education funds for military use and the Pingxiang County security group's collection of donations from school properties, were immediately stopped by telegram. (4) "Draft Regulations for Education Funding Audit Committees in Each County of Jiangxi Province": These regulations were drafted in accordance with Article 14 of the central government's measures to guarantee education funding and have been sent to each county for compliance in organization. (5) "Propose that the Financial Committees of Each County Manage Education Funding": It is proposed to follow the supplementary measures promulgated by the Ministry for the financial bureaus of each county to manage education funding. This has been approved for adoption by this headquarters. (B) Regarding planning: (1) Plan to pilot the method of raising funds for compulsory education in the relatively stable county areas of this province (Explanation): The local education funding in each county of this province has always been managed by the Education Bureau or the County Education Funding Management Committee. Since the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression issued the regulations for rectifying local finances in each county in the bandit suppression area, the original Management Committee has been taken over by the Financial Committee. Therefore, the Department can only start with investigation and review in terms of rectification, and the principle of the guarantee measures is to prohibit misappropriation." Furthermore, the education funding in each county, apart from the original properties (rental income from houses, shops, and school fields), relies solely on a portion of the land tax surcharge (7/15ths). Bandit areas have no collection at all, and counties near bandit areas have also suffered sharp declines in income. Therefore, the education funding in each county is at most tens of thousands of yuan, and at least only four or five thousand yuan. This is the general situation of local education funding in Jiangxi.

6. Situation of Implementing Compulsory Education and Promoting People's Schools, and Opinions of Responsible Persons

The situation of promoting compulsory education in Jiangxi Province is similar to that in Anhui Province, and the difficulties are also similar. Therefore, the Outline of Measures for Implementing Compulsory Education in the First Phase and the Outline of Measures for Implementing Short-Term Compulsory Education, both set by the Ministry, have not been actively implemented. Recently, Director Cheng of the Department of Education inspected northern Jiangxi and vigorously promoted short-term elementary schools. In Jiujiang, he jointly discussed methods with local gentry and scholars. Each school requires about 80 yuan of funding per term. Over a hundred schools were immediately recognized by various groups, and about 40 schools have already been established. Regarding the fundraising for compulsory education, the Department of Education has drafted ten principles and four methods, which are recorded below: (1) Take a village or a group of connected villages as a unit. (2) The number of classes needed for all school-age children in a group should be the number of classes to be set up (each class is calculated to accommodate 50 children). (3) The total cost of the classes to be set up in a group should be the amount of funding to be raised by that group (each class is calculated at 300 yuan per year). (4) The people in a group who are able to produce should bear the aforementioned expenses according to their financial strength (the burden per person should not exceed 5% of annual income). However, if there are public properties and rental income that can be allocated within a village or connected villages, they should be allocated as much as possible." There is no overall plan for the establishment and promotion of people's schools. However, in the Department of Education's Plan for Improving Education in this Province in the 22nd Year of the Republic (1933), there are several articles on the improvement direction: (1) Make full use of existing educational institutions to run people's schools, with existing teachers and senior students (limited to secondary schools and above) responsible for teaching. (2) To popularize literacy education, it should first be carried out in districts of the provincial capital and gradually promoted to each county, with the goal of implementation in all villages with more than 100 households within five years. The province currently has a small number of people's schools, and the promotion of literacy movements often fails to arouse students' interest or seek improvements in methods, so the results are not very significant.

7. Current Situation of Secondary Education for Girls and Promotion Measures

There are a total of ten public and private secondary schools for girls in Jiangxi Province. The provincial high school class for girls only exists in Nanchang. Those established by the church include Baoling in Nanchang and Ruli in Jiujiang. The provincial vocational school for girls originally had two departments: dyeing and weaving, and applied chemistry. From the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), the Department of Education plans to add the following two improvements: (1) Separate departments should be set up for sewing, weaving scarves, weaving socks, weaving cloth, and embroidery, enrolling elementary school graduates, with a time limit of one to two years as the principle. (2) The home economics department is actually in great need. The school should set up a home economics department in the next semester, focusing on family hygiene, nannies, food, and medical knowledge, enrolling junior high school students aged 15 or 16 and above. In addition to the above ten schools, there is a private women's handicraft school in Linchuan, with departments for knitting, embroidery, and weaving mats. It receives several hundred yuan in county subsidies annually, but the scale is very small. In the province as a whole, secondary schools for girls seem insufficient, and due to bandit disasters, the establishment of secondary schools for girls is mostly concentrated in northern Jiangxi. In terms of region, it seems not balanced or universal. This is the special situation of education in Jiangxi under the current special circumstances.

8. Implementation of Laws and Regulations for Elementary and Secondary Schools

The implementation of the various regulations for elementary and secondary schools promulgated by the Ministry in this province is as follows: (A) Regarding secondary schools: (1) All former public and private secondary schools that only had junior levels have been uniformly renamed junior high schools. (2) The age standards for junior and senior high school students in the province are stipulated as 12 to 18 years old for junior high school admission and 15 to 21 years old for senior high school, which differs greatly from the age limits set by the Ministry. In consideration of the facts, the province plans to continue to follow the previous regulations. (3) Since the 21st year of the Republic (1932), private secondary schools have been ordered to no longer attach normal school departments in accordance with the regulations. However, the private Baoling Girls' Secondary School and the private Jiansheng Secondary School in Nanchang still have attached normal school classes. (4) The names of all provincial and jointly established secondary schools have been uniformly corrected. Private secondary schools that still use place names have been ordered to correct them in accordance with the regulations set by the Ministry. (5) School superintendent inspection reports are planned to be handled in accordance with regulations starting in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). (6) Jointly established or county-established secondary schools have never received subsidies. The regulations for private secondary school subsidies are currently being revised, limited to those who have received subsidies and have achieved truly excellent results. (7) The review of secondary school funding has stipulated regulations for the Economic Committee and regulations for the handling of funding matters by provincial educational institutions. Recently, regulations for provincial educational institutions have been re-established. (8) Last September, the provincial government meeting resolved that all secondary schools in the province should implement a co-educational separation system. However, in areas where girls' schools have not been established, the situation may be accommodated and handled with flexibility. (9) Each junior high school has one grade director per grade, and each senior high school has one department director per department. It is planned to be corrected in accordance with the regulations set by the Ministry in the 23rd year of the Republic (1934). (10) The reorganization plan for each secondary school this year focuses on improving the quality of various facilities and has established regulations for the Unified Equipment Committee and measures for purchasing and storing equipment costs, which have already been implemented. (11) Students who fail in conduct or physical education are not allowed to participate in the graduation examination. (12) Public and private secondary schools have spring term classes, such as the Ganzhou Secondary School, Linchuan Secondary School, and Nanchang First Secondary School in the province, and private schools such as Jiansheng, Hongsheng, Zhicheng, Yaoxi, and Youyou. (13) According to the Jiangxi enrollment regulations, the number of students with equivalent academic qualifications admitted to junior high school may not exceed 10% of the total enrollment, and senior high school does not admit students with equivalent academic qualifications. However, starting in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), senior high schools are allowed to admit students who fail one or two subjects in the junior high school graduation examination as a trial, and they must still pass the supplementary examination for the failed subjects before they can become formal students. (14) The province has established regulations for scholarships and grants, which have not been implemented for long and were soon suspended due to insufficient funding. In the 21st year of the Republic (1932), these regulations were revised and are currently being implemented. (15) The principals of provincial secondary schools in the province teach six hours per week and do not receive additional pay. (16) Since the 21st year of the Republic (1932), regulations have been established to prohibit concurrent employment and salary. (17) The province's three regulations, and the province's regulations, stipulate that part-time teachers must not account for more than one-third of the total number of teachers. Starting this year, it has been changed to follow the regulations of the Ministry.

Ministry Order to Prevent Overseas Students in Japan from Fraudulently Receiving Public Funds 222

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of each province and city and the supervisory office for overseas students in Japan, stating, "The study period for publicly funded overseas students and the subsidy period for subsidized students in each province and city have been stipulated at the time of sending students abroad and approving subsidies. It has now been reported that among the overseas students receiving public funds or subsidies, there are cases where they have not actually enrolled or have already returned to the country but are still entrusting others to collect public funds or subsidies on their behalf. This should be investigated and dealt with to prevent fraud. In addition to separate distribution, you are hereby ordered to comply and report back."

Film Review Committee to Be Changed to Full-Time 223

Regarding film review matters, the Film Review Committee is jointly formed by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, with members from both ministries serving concurrently. The commissioner in charge of film matters in the Central Government has now signed and commented on the matter and submitted it to the Central Government, which has been sent to the Ministry of Education and other departments for review and reply. The original signed comments have three main points, which are roughly: (1) Members of the Film Review Committee must have a deep understanding of the Three Principles of the People and must have received higher education. (2) They must have a specialty in at least one foreign language (such as English, French, German, Japanese, etc.) (with English as the main one). (3) Committee members must be full-time. It is heard that the Ministry has expressed its agreement with this principle and will formulate measures based on the principle after a considerable period of time. In the future, film review committee members will be full-time.

Letter from Zhou Xiaozhen Jun Published as Is 224

The esteemed editor of Shen Bao,

I have read the "The Process of the Ministry of Education's Reply to Zhou Xiaozhen's Request to Issue the Tangram Phonetic Symbols," which was published in your newspaper's education news on January 12th. There are some points in it that do not match the facts, and I must request a correction. There are also some one-sided remarks that I must clarify. Since the matter is related to culture, I earnestly request that you disclose the following two main points and attachments in your newspaper to clarify the truth. (1) According to what your newspaper published, there are words such as "...the Ministry still approved the request of the National Language Unification Preparatory Committee to only allow the point of using tangrams to help practice phonetic symbols, only allow the game of phonetic symbols to be published freely, and be freely cast in lead type and printed for trial use, and when the book is published, the words 'Approved for distribution after review by the Ministry of Education' can be printed on the book..." These words do not match the facts. According to the Ministry's approval numbers 895, 930, 6036, and 9649, the phrases "free publication, free casting of lead type for printing trial use" and "the words 'Approved for distribution after review by the Ministry of Education' can be printed on the book..." refer specifically to the printed font of the Tangram Phonetic Symbols. This is something that I must request be corrected. (2) According to what your newspaper published, there are words such as "...refuting with six reasons, about a thousand words, all based on academic principles," etc. Please read Zhou Xiaozhen's 17th document submitted to the Ministry of Education to see whether it is based on logical academic principles. Moreover, its conclusion roughly states "...as for the proposed correction of the phonetic symbol printing style..." etc. To this day, the National Language Unification Preparatory Committee cannot point out which ones are slightly similar, which ones are tilted, which ones are skewed, and which ones have unclear strokes... These are all vague dismissals from three years ago, and the so-called "all based on academic principles" has not been refuted again since Xiaozhen's explanation. That is why the approval order was issued for free publication and free casting of lead type. Otherwise, since the Unification Committee had refuted it with two thousand words earlier, how could it have admitted it without reason later? This is the second point that I must clarify. After all, writing is a tool for teaching, and phonetic symbols are a tool to help recognize writing. Tools should be simple, sharp, universally applicable, and there is nothing mysterious about them. If one hears the words "Tangram" and immediately harbors contempt and aversion, and does not delve into its effectiveness, or even if it has been clearly recognized repeatedly in writing, and still cleverly denies it, as if tangrams damage dignity and nobility and are even worse than lying, then it is truly a misfortune for the future of the national language, and it is also why illiteracy in our country is not easily eliminated.

To faithfully offend the anger of the ruler, the crime is determined without pardon. Although, the Tangram Phonetic Symbols are indeed a precious raft of the national language and a savior for illiteracy. Xiaozhen has long been willing to sacrifice himself for it. Xiaozhen only knows to do his best to remove all obstacles for it, and to do his best to help it benefit the national language, benefit illiteracy, and benefit our Chinese nation. Whether the authorities pardon or not is not what I care about. Respectfully, I wish you peace. Zhou Xiaozhen bows, under the lamp on the 15th day of the first month of the 23rd year of the Republic.

Chamber of Commerce Boy Scouts to Hold Meeting Today to Commemorate Four Martyrs 225

▲ Meeting at 7 AM and Screening Films

▲ Welcome to Scouts of this city for visit

During the January 28th Shanghai War, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Troop organized a front-line stretcher team to participate in the Red Cross rescue work and a rear service team. All members were mobilized to cooperate with the military and various charitable organizations, and their work was extremely diligent. At that time, four Boy Scouts serving in the Red Cross rescue team, Luo Yunxiang, Ying Wenda, Mao Zhengxiang, and Bao Zhengwu, were sent by the Red Cross to rescue the family of a post office employee, Mr. Bai, in the war zone. They were captured by the enemy on the way and falsely accused of being spies, and tragically killed. Today marks the second anniversary of the martyrdom of the four martyrs. The troop will hold a memorial service in front of the memorial tower. In addition to representatives from the Chamber of Commerce and the Red Cross, all troop members and the families of the martyrs will attend. Scouts from this city are also welcome to attend. Students of Mawei Naval Academy

Led by Huang Xianqi to Fujian This Morning 232

During the Fujian Incident, the entire Mawei Naval Academy left the school and traveled to Beijing on the Wanxiang Wheel. It has been almost two months. Now that the Fujian Incident has been quelled, the Ministry of the Navy has ordered the students of the school to return to the Mawei Naval Academy to resume classes. Yesterday, all the students, led by the director of the school, Huang Xianqi, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing and are scheduled to take the Xinming Wheel to Fujian this morning. The situation will be reported as follows:

Renamed New President 233

The president of the Mawei Naval Academy was originally General Du Xigui, a veteran of the Navy. After Mr. Du passed away in Shanghai, the Ministry of the Navy selected Mr. Zhu Tiansen, a counselor of the Ministry, to succeed him as president. The Central Government has already been petitioned to appoint him. Zhu is from Yangzhou, Jiangsu, and has a deep reputation and knowledge in the Navy. However, because Mr. Zhu's affairs in Beijing have not been completed, he cannot go to Mawei to take office immediately. He must go to Fujian to take office in a week.

Students Leave Nanjing 234

A total of 132 students from the Naval Academy who withdrew and moved to Nanjing due to the Fujian Incident. Now that Fujian has been recovered by the Central Army and various agencies are gradually taking over and reorganizing, the Mawei Naval Academy has also been ordered to resume classes. The Ministry of the Navy has consulted with the Military Transportation Department and mobilized the China Merchants Bureau's Xinming Wheel to transport all 180 students and faculty members from Beijing to Mawei, Fujian, at 4 PM on the 29th. Classes are scheduled to resume on February 3rd.

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 235

The Xinming vessel, carrying all naval students, departed from Beijing at 4 PM on the 29th. It arrived at Xuehai yesterday afternoon. Due to the need to replenish fuel and food, the ship docked at the Jinliyuan Wharf upon arrival in Shanghai. Our reporter went to the vessel and met with Instructor Shen. He informed us that the naval students had been away from the school for two months and were now being led back to Mawei. Classes would resume immediately upon arrival. The total number of students was 132, divided into four classes. This trip was led by the Dean of Academic Affairs, Huang Xianqi. The teaching staff, including supervisors Zheng Changheng and Ye Jinqin, and instructor Chen Chenghui, totaling 24 people, also returned to the school on the same vessel.

Sailing to Mawei This Morning 236

Yesterday, the ship arrived in Shanghai to load coal and add food supplies. The crew members, having been away from Shanghai for a long time, also reported to the bureau about their duties in Beijing. The students and teaching staff remained on board, awaiting departure. It was scheduled to set sail from Shanghai at 4 AM this morning, heading directly for Mawei, Fujian. It is expected to arrive on Friday morning. It is said that a large number of books, instruments, and curriculum materials taken out of the school when the students left are now being carried back to the school by the Xinming vessel. The new principal, Zhu Tiansen, is said to be scheduled to come to Shanghai from Beijing within the next week to wait for the ship to go to Mawei and formally take over the position of principal.

Second Phase of City Education Association's Inspection of Private Schools Completed 237

The Shanghai City Education Association has sponsored more than twenty private schools this semester. To assess the performance of each school, the association divided the schools into phases for members of the board of directors and supervisors to inspect. It is now known that the second phase of inspection work has been completed. The results of the inspection show that the performance of the second and ninth private schools are the most outstanding.

Conditions of the Shanghai Municipal Council Public Library 238

The director of the Shanghai Municipal Council Public Library stated in the work report for 1933 that on May 1st of that year, the library moved to the upper floors of the Biefa Bookstore Company at 22 Nanjing Road. The new location occupies 4,000 square feet of floor space, with excellent lighting and sufficient space. It is divided into three rooms: one is a general reading room, where magazines and newspapers are placed and is free for public access; one is a subscription reading room, which provides newspapers, magazines, and reference books; and one is a book room, which occupies the most space and includes the catalog and lending desk. All rooms are equipped with heating, so readers can be comfortable. Regarding the acquisition of books, the cost of purchasing books was 2,400 taels, acquiring 393 novels, 165 general books, and 66 children's books. At the end of the year, the latest edition of the Encyclopedia Britannica and 40 new books on economics and finance were purchased for reference. A total of 1,200 books have been bound. Cataloging and recataloging work is in progress. Because there are 20,000 books in stock and they are constantly being borrowed, the cataloging work requires a long period of systematic effort. This year, 150 volumes were purchased thanks to donations. Mr. Yan E-sheng of the City Chamber of Commerce donated 3,800 volumes of Chinese books, which are now stored in newly made bookshelves. The Zilin Newspaper Office donated 11 books. There are many borrowers. Also, someone donated a complete set of "Historians' History," which has been placed in the reference room. This year, there are 65 Chinese and 535 foreign subscribers, totaling 600 people. The number of books borrowed is 54,121 novels and 6,671 other books. The library is now equipped with a public telephone, so that conversations will not disturb readers.

Expansion of the City Chamber of Commerce Library and Reading Room 241

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce Commercial Library Reading Room was originally located on the second floor, which was narrow, poorly lit, and quite unsuitable. The reading room has also been greatly expanded, so that there will be no overcrowding. The reading time has now been changed to start at 10 AM, while the reading time is still from 12:30 PM to 8 PM. However, borrowing books still requires a reader's card.

School News 242

▲Huzhou Girls' Middle School The Huzhou Girls' Middle School in Huzhou was founded in the late Qing Dynasty and has a long history. It is known for its strict teaching and high reputation. The magnificence of the school buildings and the perfection of the facilities are rare among middle schools in the interior. During the recent winter vacation, it has further expanded and added more than twenty bathrooms, and also drilled an artesian well and installed motors and hot and cold water pipes for the use of all faculty and students. Enrollment was originally scheduled for January 22nd, but because students from distant places have sent letters to register and requested an extension, it has now been specifically scheduled for February 10th as the second examination date. Hills is the American Netball King

Jickel Is the Netball Queen 250

Mrs. Maddy's Throne Dethroned

Vannes Falls Behind

| Netball Rankings for 1933 |

(New York, 29th National Telegram) According to the rankings for 1933 announced by the American Lawn Netball Association, Hills is the American Netball King, and Ms. Jickel is the Netball Queen.

Vannes Not Listed 251

The committee's choice of the top two is not surprising. Since Vannes's collapse and subsequent turn to professionalism, there is no doubt that he will no longer be included in the rankings. With Vannes gone, Hills stands out, winning five major championship tournaments, including Siblatd, Newpode, and Samsondun. Hills is also the semi-finalist in the All-American Congress.

Overcoming Mrs. Maddy 252

There is also no question that Ms. Jickel, having won the All-American Netball Congress Women's Championship, is ranked first. Her victory over Mrs. Maddy makes Ms. Jickel's throne even more valuable. The top spot is not a problem, but there is much discussion about Ellison being ranked second. The "short-necked" Ellison has not won a championship in the country, and his performance in the Davis Cup can be said to be equal to zero. The two or three people below him have better results than Ellison.

Questions About Women's Rankings 253

Other criticisms include Ms. Mable's ranking of third and Mrs. Faifley's ranking of fourth. Although Ms. Ma won the Mei Shidong Championship, Mrs. Faifley also won the Siblatuo Championship, which Ms. Jickel also participated in. Her replacement of Mrs. Maddy in the Deerman Cup also created a special record.

Stoke Fen Made the Most Progress 254

The fastest-improving player is Stoke Fen. He was not listed in 1930, was ranked fifteenth in 1931, rose to sixth place last year, and jumped to third place this year. His future is unlimited. Hills's rapid progress is also amazing. His European tour was canceled last spring, and his performance was extremely poor. Hills worked hard and swept the Eastern Championships, like a landmine exploding, until he was eliminated by Crawford in the semi-finals of the All-American Congress. Rodd and Stoke Fen's doubles are also ranked first in the All-American Men's Doubles. The men's and women's rankings are as follows:

Free Talk

The Decay of Lying by Yu Dafu 257

—

"The Decay of Lying" is the title of an essay written in dialogue form by the aesthete Wilde. He criticized realism, recalled the illusory world of beauty in ancient times, and believed that the art of lying and fabricating rumors had declined to the point of extinction in modern times. Therefore, his contemporaries and the slightly older predecessor, Flaubert, were mocked by his aphorisms. He said that the reason why Americans have not created good literature is because their founding fathers did not know how to lie. The legend of Washington chopping down the cherry tree is a toxin that stifles the creative instincts of Americans.

Whether Wilde's exaggerated views are correct or not has already been discussed by many literary critics, so we will not bother with it for the time being. Looking back at the literati of China, both ancient and modern, I feel that they are indeed much less advanced than Westerners in the art of lying and fabricating rumors. King Cheng cutting tung leaves into jade tablets and playfully enfeoffing Shuyu was such an interesting and elegant affair, but Duke Zhou was too serious, and the best lie was exposed. Zhao Gao pointing at a deer and calling it a horse was also a good trick, but he had to add executions behind it to achieve a practical result. An interesting thing became a bad thing.

In modern times, this art of lying has become even more atrocious to the extreme. News reports often expose themselves because of lying, and the fabrication of rumors and lies in small publications is naturally even worse. To say nothing else, let's just talk about the reports about me personally. One publication just said that I was running around in Hangzhou, currying favor with third- and fourth-rate politicians, and got a job as a newspaper editor for thirty yuan a month; at the same time, another publication said that I was composing poems in the snow, and my leisure and elegance had reached an unparalleled level. In order to make this lie seem like the truth, this gentleman even racked his brains and made up several new and not-so-new, old and not-so-old, very original poems about snow for me. Do you think that with the art of spreading rumors declining to such a degree, can the Chinese nation still create great works?

On the Theory That Art Is Life 258

— Lin Huiyin

Now that new literature no longer needs to exert effort in dealing with old literature, new literature itself has formed two major factions: (1) The "art for art's sake" faction, and (2) the "art for life's sake" faction.

The "art for art's sake" faction says that artistic creation is only for the sake of art itself, and definitely not for any other purpose. The "art for life's sake" faction, however, says that art is not just for art's sake, but to improve the current situation or advance society. However, although these two factions once debated fiercely without yielding, it has now become a thing of the past and no longer shows any traces of contention. Moreover, although someone may occasionally bring it up, the two factions of "art for art's sake" and "art for life's sake" no longer seem to be in clear opposition.

However, what I want to say now is not about the past disputes between the two factions, but that artistic creation can never be solely for the sake of art. Artistic creation is for life, but not necessarily for the general life as the "art for life's sake" faction says, but for the creator's own life.

Yes, the creator's creation is part of the creator's life.

Now, let's take literature and art as an example. When a novelist writes a novel and publishes it somewhere, his purpose is always either for fame or for profit, or, at least, to vent his inner depression or anger. In short, the reason he writes it is nothing more than to satisfy a certain desire of his own, so it cannot but be a part of his life. Even if he writes it and does not publish it, but tears it up, burns it, or buries it in the soil, it is also a kind of life for him, because he does so to seek satisfaction of one of his desires.

Will a novelist who writes for fame or profit fail to become a novelist? No, there is no reason for him not to become a novelist, if his novel is a good novel, a crystallization of his own hard work, and a powerful work that can move people. We know that many of Balzac's works in "The Human Comedy" were forced out of him because he had to pay off debts, but that did not hinder the artistic value of his works.

Therefore, a work should be judged on its own merits, and the motive for writing it, whether for fame or profit, is not of great importance. Moreover, the creator's motive for creation always has a source, even if it is not necessarily in fame or profit, because it cannot but be a part of his life.

Snow 259

— Hei Ding

On snowy days, I think of home.

A heart like a breaking wave, impossible to settle. Depressed eyes, staring at the snowflakes outside the window, falling one by one. Life is like the falling snowflakes. Wandering dreams, lost youth, solitary trek on this gloomy path of life. It has been more than two years since I went home. It is already deep winter, my body is bleakly cold, and my heart is also bleakly cold! I just think: the snow in my hometown must be falling in large swathes, covering the whole earth in white. I love the snow in my hometown, the snow in my hometown hides the spring of my childhood.

However, the snow in my hometown is now stained with scarlet blood! We must not lightly forget that lost free home!

I can't help but say it's a sad thing, since the September 18th Incident, the home has been broken, and the people at home have been exiled, so I slowly forgot about home! Then, with the strength of life, I began to tread firmly and embark on the road forward.

My heart is warm, and I am looking forward to the light of the future!

Sometimes, my heart smiles and whispers: Quickly follow the wheels of history and turn to a new stage!

So, I was reborn.

I have no home. I wander everywhere. I have identified a direction.

I have tasted a lot of the bitterness of life alone; this journey of life is so long and far!

Often a little stimulation makes me neglect my progress, which is my greatest shortcoming! However, I always remember that people must move forward to be able to live.

I have already forged myself into a person who is used to living an alien life. But at the same time, I have also become a melancholy person; I didn't smile in spring, I didn't smile in summer, and I didn't smile even more in autumn. In winter, I stare at the snowflakes outside the window, adding to my sorrow!

Whenever a deep winter comes, my heart has to encounter a heavy illness, and I grieve even more at the white snow!

Now, the winter is deep in Qingdao, where I am staying, and my heart is also heavily ill! I can't help but sing a lament to this first snow.

So, I thought of home.

Home, has already sunk into the Northeast, which has become "Manchukuo"! The deep winter in the Northeast must be a beautiful world of snow!

Impressions of the Burmese 260

— Liu Ming

On the way from Xiaotianba at the foot of the Savage Mountain directly to Bamo, the Burmese driving the passenger car suddenly stopped the car and jumped into the forest beside the road. What are they doing? The passengers opened their curious eyes and looked, oh, it turned out that the Burmese was touched by the sound of cicadas in the forest and was interestingly searching for the sobbing cicada.

This is my first impression of the Burmese. Although it is very ordinary, it made me pay deep attention to them, and I have not forgotten it until now. That was in the spring of 1927. (If we talk about Myanmar, there is no spring, we should only say it is the dry season). When I go to a place, I always like to study the temperament of those foreigners, and I like to compare the people I have contacted before, to find out their differences. Because this is the joy of traveling, I am happy to do so.

I think the Burmese are younger than the Chinese nation, and they have a strong childish and playful temperament. In Mandalay (the old capital of Myanmar) and in Yangon, I have seen that if there are a few Burmese young people walking around the streets, it is not difficult to encounter the entertaining things of singing and clapping hands. As for the public buses running in the city, the happy situation of the Burmese people riding in them, reaching out from the windows to clap and shout, sometimes flashes across the tree-lined streets, arousing the surprise and smiles of distant travelers.

We Chinese are not like this, we are always solemn and quiet. Even at the most joyful times, like celebrating the Lunar New Year, there is still no unrestrained singing and wanton playfulness. Ordinary people, especially farmers in the countryside, on the contrary, dress neatly on New Year's Day and become pretentious. Probably today's inland farmhouses still have such couplets posted in front of their doors: "Everyone acts like a gentleman, everywhere there is a style of yielding and courtesy." Isn't this a good portrayal of the New Year?

In Myanmar, I have encountered several Burmese New Years, and those happy days are around mid-April in the Gregorian calendar. What do you think those Burmese people with childish temperaments play? Oh, they carry buckets and ladles, gather in the streets and alleys, and when they see people wearing new clothes, regardless of men and women, regardless of old and young, they splash a ladle of cold water on your head, followed by again and again, again and again, until you immediately become a miserable sight like a drowned dog. If you are sitting in a tram or car, water will also fly in from the window. On these days (only three days), water flowers are flying everywhere, overflowing with laughter, and the Burmese are all as happy as if they were crazy.

When I return to China, I often feel that everything around me is too dull, too old, and the blood of young people must be injected.

Dream of Hometown 261

— Huan Ming

In recent years, the types of dreams have gradually become more numerous, but in these dreams of mine, there are very few about my hometown. In the past, although I had many dreams about my hometown, that was in my childhood. The period when I dreamed about my hometown the most was in the one or two years not long after I left my hometown. What I dreamed of was nothing more than those elders who loved me and the material satisfaction that I could not enjoy outside. After waking up, I would clamor to return to my hometown, even crying.

As the days went by, I became accustomed to the life outside; the dreams of my hometown also diminished like my longing for my hometown. Although I still dreamed about it occasionally, the hometown I dreamed of was already decorated with cars and carriages, and even the streets of my hometown were asphalt.

When I told my father about this kind of dream, he was dumbfounded: in fact, there were no rickshaws in my hometown, and he sighed sadly:

"You have forgotten your home, you have been away for too long, one should not forget one's roots..."

So, I returned to my hometown that winter.

As a result, I left my hometown before I had lived there for two weeks. Since then, I have rarely dreamed about my hometown. Maybe I occasionally have this kind of dream, but none of them can arouse my lingering feelings. Everything in the dream hometown is vulgar, old, and the roads are uneven (more uneven than the real hometown). After waking up, I feel depressed and unhappy, even ashamed to recall it.

People are originally like this, and the evolution of society is precisely because people can be like this. The evolution of society is a contradictory cycle. After being tired of the turning of the wheels and the clamor of the city, I began to dream of my hometown again. My hometown is quietly unfolding in my dream: green trees, flowing water, fields, and the twittering of birds! My hometown is beautiful.

My hometown is probably covered in white snow now, I think. When my hometown really appears before my eyes, I will definitely be disappointed, but I have decided to return to my hometown again. Life is originally a contradictory deception, people say: "The purpose of life is not in the purpose itself, but in the process." Then, on the way home, I think I can always satisfy my hometown's wish for me.

Before Sunrise (3) 262

— Gao Zhi

Lian Di became even more shy listening to this.

"Third Aunt, it's hard to say at this point. There's no other way. Lian Di, light the lamp."

"This world can't be said like that anymore. Times have changed. Our Madam was raised by the third wife, and isn't she enjoying blessings? In the mansion, the status may be a little lower, but life is always good, and there's no shortage of clothes, food, or anything else."

Lian Di didn't understand and went to light the lamp. She felt a bit of novelty, thinking that her mother had brought back a rare guest from burning incense in the city, which was really rare.

A large wisp of black smoke rose from the flame of the small bottle-shaped kerosene lamp without a lampshade. The light was very weak. The Zhong Kui in the dusty hall looked like a piece of old paper, and people's shadows were vaguely reflected on the wall. Aunt Qin and Third Aunt were whispering.

Aunt Qin's mysterious air made Lian Di feel a little strange, and Lian Di was also surprised why Third Aunt was also so secretive. She only saw one side of Third Aunt. She had the shrewdness of city people, dressed neatly, and the golden earrings hanging from her earlobes shone with a lovely light. Compared to Aunt Qin, she was much more glamorous.

"Lian Di looks really delicate. Lian Di, Third Aunt says you are lucky, remember that."

Third Aunt smiled and looked at Lian Di. Lian Di was only seventeen years old. Due to the operation of various farm and household chores, her body was developing very well. She originally had a very sturdy body, but she had been enduring famine for too long recently and had become thin. She had good looks, with a round face carrying the innocence and shyness of a young girl. The young men of Yuhua Village called her "Sister Hua". Although she was thin recently, it made her appear slender. Third Aunt thought that if she could eat and dress well again, wouldn't she become a beauty after a while?

Listening to this, Lian Di felt at a loss, and the eyes under her slender eyebrows were shyly about to close. She twisted her body shyly and walked into the dark little room.

She really couldn't bear for her daughter to leave her, but could she let her starve to death in the countryside? What could she do if she couldn't bear it? She couldn't help complaining to Third Aunt, saying that the days were getting harder and harder, and they always relied on the harvest from the land, but it was getting worse every year, and the harvest from the land was never enough to live on. "Third Aunt, we can't rely on the land anymore, what can we rely on?"

"I heard that relief wheat is going to be distributed, but I don't know when."

"It doesn't count until it's distributed. If it's distributed earlier, my daughter won't leave. If we wait any longer, aren't we just waiting to starve to death?"

"Aunt Qin, rely on Lian Di. Look at it later."

In the evening, Lian Di felt very uneasy in front of Third Aunt. She thought: Why is Third Aunt always looking at me? What is she looking at me for? Mom also looks a little strange, does she have something on her mind? Why does she want to say it but not say it, and she seems happy and unhappy at the same time? Why is Third Aunt always smiling? Lian Di didn't understand and couldn't figure it out.

Aunt Qin hesitated several times before stuttering:

"Lian Di, you go to the city tomorrow to borrow rice, go with Third Aunt."

This unexpected news made Lian Di very happy. She raised her head and said excitedly:

"Mom, how much to borrow? How much to borrow? I'll go, I'll go."

Lian Di's joy was what Aunt Qin expected, but she had to say what Third Aunt said:

"Just carry as much as you can. If you can carry three dou, then three dou, if you can carry five dou, then five dou. Don't be impatient when you get to the city, other people's rice isn't waiting there for us to eat. Listen to Third Aunt, it doesn't matter if it takes three or five days. Come back when you have the rice."

"Mom, I can carry six dou, look, I can still walk carrying a load of rice." Lian Di was a little carried away.

"Just carry as much as you can. But don't overwhelm yourself."

"Okay, okay." Lian Di thought, if I could carry back a load, that would be great. But even a cloth bag would be considerable.

Lian Di smiled because of her mother's words, and her mother and Third Aunt smiled because the idea was sold. Lian Di saw them smiling and looking at her at the same time, especially Third Aunt's sharp eyes, as if she wanted to find something on her face. She was afraid that a small scar by her hair and a black mole above her ear would be seen by Third Aunt, so she shyly turned her head away and felt uneasy.

After Third Aunt went to sleep, Lian Di whispered to her mother about her curiosity about Third Aunt. Her mother said that Third Aunt had gone to the city, gotten lucky, and made a fortune. Lian Di said in an envious tone in a low voice:

Gold Standard Drops and Then Rises

Rumors Spread that Britain and the United States Will Discuss Currency

Market Situation Firm and Rebounds by One Yuan

Although the gold market was weak at the opening yesterday, it ended up falling and then rising. Yarn and Cotton

Not Much January Yarn and Cotton Delivery 270

Only 700 Bales of Yarn and 15,500 Piculs of Cotton

The auction of January yarn started on August 1st of last year, with a price of 195.6 yuan. Later, due to disappointing autumn sales, rural decline, and economic hardship, yarn sales became increasingly sluggish. In addition, foreign yarns were being dumped from all sides, and the production and sales areas of Chinese yarn were invaded. Chinese yarn became increasingly surplus, inventory continued to rise, and the market showed increasing cracks, trending downwards step by step, directly breaking through the 180 yuan mark. On October 16th, a cotton industry organization was established to maintain the market price, which rebounded to 186-187 yuan. However, actual demand remained sluggish. It was heard that the Zhejiang military situation was serious, and that a large factory and a certain association's long positions had no intention of taking delivery, and were settling at the market price. With this large amount of chips being dumped, it was like a dam collapsing, and the price plummeted to 173-174 yuan in two or three days. Moreover, there were very large changes, and the struggle between long and short positions was fierce. According to market rumors, the exchange's shareholder group organized to maintain a limited price of 170 yuan for the near-term yarn delivery, and sold it externally. The market was temporarily stabilized by this, rising slightly to 74.4 yuan. By the middle of this month, due to weak actual demand and long positions settling, the final session was still at 170 yuan. As a result, 700 bales remained, and only 250 bales of 20-count "San Yang" yarn were actually delivered. The rest was self-delivered. The January term "Zheng Biao" cotton was listed on August 1st of last year, with a price of 44.05 yuan. It rose slightly to 4.23 yuan. Although the US Department of Agriculture had implemented a plan to destroy one-quarter of the cotton fields, the harvest was abundant, and the market was still difficult to stabilize. On August 8th, the government announced that the production situation was good, and the market price fell, causing a unified shock in the world cotton market. At the same time, the price of rice and paddy in China was low, farmers increased cotton fields, rainfall was favorable, and cotton production was abundant. The market fell step by step, breaking through the 40 yuan mark in mid-October. The lowest was 38.5 yuan. Later, the moisture content of the new cotton was too high, and although there was a source, the delivery did not match. At the end of the year, the problem of cotton industry between Japan and India was resolved. Indian cotton first rose, and US cotton also rose. The market was excited, and the auction cotton rose from 39.8 yuan straight to over 42 yuan. By the end of the month, there was still no sufficient chips on the delivery side. The final peak price was 42.4 yuan, 2.6 yuan higher than last month's price. As a result, 15,500 piculs remained, and the delivery price was 42 yuan. Among them, 5,000 piculs were self-delivered. North Shanghai Again Stopped Measurement Yesterday 275

Carters and Porters Restarted Their Dispute

South Shanghai Long-grained Rice Continued to Rise by 0.05 Yuan as a Result

Yesterday, the source of each gang in South Shanghai was more than 30 (nearly 5,000 "shi" - a unit of dry volume), and the market situation was tight because the dock workers in Zhabei were competing for work and holding each other back, causing the industry in the north of the city to shut down entirely. However, the actual situation was still normal. Only the sellers seemed to have the intention of raising prices. As a result, the long-grained rice of Chang Bang Su and Tong was raised by 0.05 yuan. As for the late rice of Qingjiao Songjiang and Jiangxi Lian, the retail market was still weak. The sales were heavily reliant on the Yang-style gangs in the north and south, and there were continued transactions of 2,000+ bales. The market situation was excellent, and the price rose by 0.5 "chi" (a unit of length, also used here as price per unit). However, Du Jiao Yang and other patterns were average, and there was not much difference between Yin-styled and plain styles. In North Shanghai, at about 9 AM yesterday, a few firms opened for measurement. As the carters were working, the porters suddenly started to fight over the trade. Both sides clashed and bled, and several people were injured. The firms could not open for measurement because of this, and they successively closed down to prevent accidents. After the Public Security Bureau sent police to maintain order, each firm waited for the Rice Association to resolve the matter before they could resume as normal. So there was no market report.

Guest-origin Glutinous Rice Rose Again Outward 276

Fuzhou-Style Operations Very Dense

Merchants Unwilling to Let Go Easily

Yesterday, the gate of the guest-origin long-grained rice became more and more active. Because the "Zha" style operations were done by the local guest gangs, the market has continued to rise, so it has been hard to get into the game. The Quanzhou gang has also not competed, so the market has been solely led by the provincial gang. However, merchants said that in recent days, sources have not been prosperous, and the product price has gradually increased. Since there would be very few shipments at the end of the lunar year, most refuse to sell off. The market has become more tense. Yesterday's city Xian Yuan and other rice types have all risen outward, across the board. About 4,500 bales were sold in the city, but only 100+ bales were purchased by Ji Jing here. All the rest was operated by the Min provincial gang. The after-market is still bullish. Because the Min gang still has a big appetite, it may be enough to shake the market, speaking only of the Fuzhou gang. Furthermore, there is the need for the Quanzhou gangs to continue to inquire, so the market and market sentiment all have the hope of expansion.
